---
layout: "post"
title: "HoTT exercises"
date: "2018-04-08"
categories: type-theory
toc: true
---

This is a self-contained version of some solutions for HoTT-Book's exercises.
The idea is to unpackage all as long as possible to get a better understanding.
Many changes can appear running this experiment. Solutions are
type-checked as a whole using Agda v2.5.3.

## Requirements

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Agda has a pragma to work with HoTT:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="516" class="Symbol">{-#</a> <a id="520" class="Keyword">OPTIONS</a> <a id="528" class="Option">--without-K</a> <a id="540" class="Symbol">#-}</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Equality type definition also called Identity type:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="703" class="Keyword">infix</a> <a id="709" class="Number">4</a> <a id="711" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">_≡_</a>

## Chapter 1

### Exercise 1.1

{: .exercise}
  Given functions $$f : A \to B$$ and $$g:B\to C$$, define
  their composite $$ g\circ f:A\to C$$.
  Show that we have $$h \circ (g\circ f) \equiv (h\circ g)\circ f$$.


We define the composition operation in Agda as follows.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="_∘_" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%88%98_" class="Function Operator">_∘_</a> <a id="2104" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2106" class="Symbol">∀</a> <a id="2108" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="2109" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2109" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="2111" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2111" class="Bound">j</a> <a id="2113" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2113" class="Bound">k</a><a id="2114" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="2116" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="2117" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2117" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="2119" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2121" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="2125" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2109" class="Bound">i</a><a id="2126" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="2128" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2128" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="2130" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2132" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="2136" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2111" class="Bound">j</a><a id="2137" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="2139" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2139" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="2141" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2143" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="2147" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2113" class="Bound">k</a><a id="2148" class="Symbol">}</a>
    <a id="2154" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2156" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="2157" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2128" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="2159" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2161" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2139" class="Bound">C</a><a id="2162" class="Symbol">)</a>
    <a id="2168" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2170" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="2171" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2117" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="2173" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2175" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2128" class="Bound">B</a><a id="2176" class="Symbol">)</a>
    <a id="2182" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2184" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2117" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="2186" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2188" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2139" class="Bound">C</a>
<a id="2190" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2190" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="2192" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%88%98_" class="Function Operator">∘</a> <a id="2194" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2194" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="2196" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="2198" class="Symbol">λ</a> <a id="2200" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2200" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="2202" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2204" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2190" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="2206" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="2207" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2194" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="2209" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2200" class="Bound">x</a><a id="2210" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Then, the `∘-assoc` shows us that associativity of this composition holds.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="∘-assoc" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%88%98-assoc" class="Function">∘-assoc</a> <a id="2321" class="Symbol">:</a> <a ### Exercise 1.2

<div class="exercise">
Derive the recursion principle for products $$\mathsf{rec}_{A\times B}$$
using only the projections, and verify that the definitional equalities
are valid. Do the same for $$\Sigma$$-types.
</div>

To solve this problem we need to know:

  - The recursion principle for Σ-types:

    <p class="equation">
    $$ \mathsf{rec}_{ A \times B}
      : \prod\limits_{C : \mathcal{U}} (A \to B \to C) → A \times B \to C.
    $$
    </p>

  - The recursion principle for Σ-types:

    <p class="equation">
    $$ \mathsf{rec}_{\sum\limits_{(x : A) } B(x)}
      : \prod\limits_{(C : U)} (\Pi_{(x : A)} B(x) \rightarrow C) \rightarrow
        \sum_{(x : A)} B(x) \rightarrow C
    $$
    </p>

<div class="proof" id="proof-1.2">
Proof.<br/>
For products:<br/>
If we have the projections,
$$\mathsf{proj}_1 : A \times B \to \mathsf{A}$$ and $$\mathsf{proj}_2 : A \times B \to \mathsf{B}$$,
then $$\mathsf{rec}_2$$ is another inhabitant where

<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
&\mathsf{rec}_1 : \prod\limits_{C : \mathcal{U}} (A \to B \to C) \to A \times B \to C\\
&\mathsf{rec}_1~C~g~c~:\equiv~g~(\mathsf{proj}_1 c,~\mathsf{proj}_2 c).
\end{align*}
$$
</p>
By reflexivity, we prove the equality between $$\mathsf{rec}_{ A \times B}$$ and $$\mathsf{rec}_1$$.
<br/>
<br/>
For sums:<br/>
The projections are $$\mathsf{proj}_1 : \sum_{x : A}  Bx \to \mathsf{A}$$ and
$$\mathsf{proj}_2 :  \prod_{(p : \sum_{x : A}  Bx)} \to \mathsf{B} (\mathsf{proj}_1 p)$$.<br/>
By using these projections, we got another recursor defined as follows:
<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{aling*}
&\mathsf{rec}_2 : \prod\limits_{C : \mathcal{U}}  (\prod_{x : A} Bx \to C) \to \sum\limits_{x : A} B x \to C\\
&\mathsf{rec}_2~C~g~c~=~g~(\mathsf{proj}_1 c)~(\mathsf{proj}_2 c)
\end{align*}
$$
</p>

By reflexivity, we prove the equality between $$\mathsf{rec}_{\sum\limits_{(x : A) } B(x)}$$ and $$\mathsf{rec}_2$$.
</div>

the following exercises including this one:

Its recursor with a function $$g : \prod_{(x : A)} B(x)\rightarrow C$$
that we provide.

  <a id="5324" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="5329" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81" class="Module">Σ-Def₁</a> <a id="5336" class="Keyword">using</a> <a id="5342" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="5343" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3" class="Record">Σ</a> <a id="5345" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="5347" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3.proj%E2%82%81" class="Field">proj₁</a><a id="5352" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="5354" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3.proj%E2%82%82" class="Field">proj₂</a><a id="5359" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="5361" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">_,_</a> <a id="5365" class="Symbol">)</a>

  <a id="Σ-Rec₁.rec" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Rec%E2%82%81.rec" class="Function">rec</a> <a id="5374" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="5376" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3" class="Record">Σ</a> <a id="5378" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#5241" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="5380" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#5252" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="5382" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="5384" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#5267" class="Bound">C</a>

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

On the other hand, the product type is just a particular case of the sigma type
when the codomain is not dependent, as we can see next by omitting the argument
in `(λ _ → B)`.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="5770" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="×-Def₁" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%81" class="Module">×-Def₁</a> <a id="5784" class="Keyword">where</a>

Its recursor with a function $$g : A \rightarrow B \rightarrow C$$ that we provide.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="6006" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="×-Rec₁" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Rec%E2%82%81" ### Exercise 1.3

<p class="exercise">
Derive the induction principle for products $$\mathsf{ind}_{A\times B}$$,
using only the projections and the propositional uniqueness principle
$$\mathsf{uniq}_{A\times B}$$.
Verify that the definitional equalities are valid.
</p>

To solve this problem, recall the uniqueness principle (Pp. 29. HoTT-Book)

- The **propositional uniqueness principle** says that
every element of $$A\times B$$ is equal to a pair.

<p class="equation">
  $$ \mathsf{uniq}_{A\times B}
     : \prod_{(x : A \times B)} ((\mathsf{proj}_{1}(x) , \mathsf{proj}_{2}(x))
       \equiv_{A\times B} x).
  $$
</p>

Product type definition using `data`:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="6937" class="Comment">-- this would be trivial in agda due to definitional η for records</a>
<a id="7004" class="Comment">-- so Capriotti defined a product type without η:</a>
<a id="7054" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="×-Def₂" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82" class="Module">×-Def₂</a> <a id="7068" class="Keyword">where</a>

  <a id="7826" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Fun%E2%82%82.ap-proj%E2%82%82" class="Function">ap-proj₂</a> <a id="7835" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a> <a id="7840" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="7842" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a>

        <a id="7900" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="7902" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7873" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="7904" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="7906" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7875" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="7908" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="7910" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7883" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="7912" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="7914" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7885" class="Bound">z</a> <a id="7916" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="7918" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="7919" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7873" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="7921" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="7923" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7883" class="Bound">y</a><a id="7924" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="7926" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="7928" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="7929" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7875" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="7931" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="7933" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7885" class="Bound">z</a><a id="7934" class="Symbol">)</a>
  <a id="7938" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Fun%E2%82%82.pair%3D" class="Function">pair=</a> <a id="7944" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a> <a id="7949" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a> <a id="7954" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="7956" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

The induction principle for the product type:

<p class="equation">
$$\mathsf{ind}_{A\times B} : \prod\limits_{C : A \times B \to \mathcal{U}}
  \left( \prod\limits_{x:A}\ \prod\limits_{y:B}\ \,C( (x,y) ) \right)
  \to \prod\limits_{x:A \times B}\ \,C(x)
$$
</p>

          <a id="8571" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="8573" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8574" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8574" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="8576" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8578" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8579" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8579" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8581" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8583" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8270" class="Bound">A</a><a id="8584" class="Symbol">)(</a><a id="8586" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8586" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="8588" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8590" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8281" class="Bound">B</a><a id="8591" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="8593" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="8595" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8542" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="8597" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8598" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8579" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8600" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="8602" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8586" class="Bound">y</a><a id="8603" class="Symbol">))</a>
          <a id="8616" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="8618" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8619" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8619" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8621" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8623" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8270" class="Bound">A</a><a id="8624" class="Symbol">)(</a><a id="8626" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8626" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="8628" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8630" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8281" class="Bound">B</a><a id="8631" class="Symbol">)</a>
          <a id="8643" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="8645" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Ind%E2%82%82.ind" class="Function">ind</a> <a id="8649" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8542" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="8651" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8574" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="8653" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8654" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8619" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8656" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="8658" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8626" class="Bound">y</a><a id="8659" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="8661" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="8663" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8574" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="8665" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8619" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8667" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8626" class="Bound">y</a>
  <a id="8671" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Ind%E2%82%82.ind-%CE%B2" class="Function">ind-β</a> <a id="8677" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8677" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="8679" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8679" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="8681" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8681" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8683" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8683" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="8685" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="8687" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

<p class="exercise">
Generalize $$\mathsf{uniq}_{A\times B}$$ to Σ-types, and do the same for
$$\Sigma$$-types, i.e. show induction and verify the definitional equality
is valid.
</p>

Σ-type definition using `data`:

    <a id="Σ-Def₂.Σ._,_" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%82.%CE%A3._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">_,_</a> <a id="9025" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9027" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="9028" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9028" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="9030" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9032" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8971" class="Bound">A</a><a id="9033" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="9035" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="9037" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8982" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="9039" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9028" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="9041" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="9043" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%82.%CE%A3" class="Datatype">Σ</a> <a id="9045" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8971" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="9047" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8982" class="Bound">B</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Its induction principle:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="9430" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="Σ-Ind₂" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Ind%E2%82%82" class="Module">Σ-Ind₂</a> <a id="9444" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="9445" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9445" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="9447" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9447" class="Bound">j</a><a id="9448" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="9450" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9450" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="9452" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9454" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="9458" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9445" class="Bound">i</a><a id="9459" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="9461" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9461" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="9463" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9465" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9450" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="9467" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="9469" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="9473" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9447" class="Bound">j</a><a id="9474" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="9476" class="Keyword">where</a>
  <a id="9484" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="9489" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%82" class="Module">Σ-Def₂</a> <a id="9496" class="Keyword">public</a>

### Exercise 1.4

<div class="exercise">
Assuming as given only the <em>iterator</em> for natural numbers
<p class="equation">
$$\mathsf{ite} : \prod\limits_{C:\mathcal{U}} C \to (C \to C) \to \mathbb{N} \to C $$
</p>
with the defining equations
<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
\mathsf{ite}(C,c_0,c_s,0)               &\equiv c_0, \\
\mathsf{ite}(C,c_0,c_s,\mathsf{suc}(n)) &\equiv c_s(\mathsf{ite}(C,c_0,c_s,n)),
\end{align*}
$$
</p>
derive a function having the type of the recursor $$\mathsf{rec}$$.
Show that the defining equations of the recursor hold propositionally for this
function, using the induction principle for $$\mathbb{N}$$.
</div>

To solve this problem, let us define the recursor and also the induction principle
for natural numbers. (See more details about these functions in
[Induction on Natural Numbers]({% post_url 2018-02-12-induction-on-natural-numbers %})).

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="10748" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="ℕ-Def" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def" class="Module">ℕ-Def</a> <a id="10761" class="Keyword">where</a>

    <a id="ℕ-Def.ℕ.suc" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95.suc" class="InductiveConstructor">suc</a>  <a id="10811" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="10813" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a> <a id="10815" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="10817" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a>

  <a id="10992" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="10997" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def" class="Module">ℕ-Def</a>

       <a id="11034" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="11036" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11037" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11014" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="11039" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95.zero" class="InductiveConstructor">zero</a><a id="11043" class="Symbol">)</a>
       <a id="11052" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="11054" class="Symbol">(∀</a> <a id="11057" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11058" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11058" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="11060" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="11062" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a><a id="11063" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="11065" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="11067" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11014" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="11069" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11058" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="11071" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="11073" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11014" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="11075" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11076" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95.suc" class="InductiveConstructor">suc</a> <a id="11080" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11058" class="Bound">n</a><a id="11081" class="Symbol">))</a>

Now, we define the iterator following the equations above:

Then, we now can define the recursor using this `ite` by iterating over the type
`ℕ × C` (*reloading recursion*?).


<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="11601" class="Comment">-- recursor</a>
  <a id="11615" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="11620" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82" class="Module">×-Def₂</a> <a id="11627" class="Keyword">using</a> <a id="11633" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11634" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_" class="Datatype Operator">_×_</a><a id="11637" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="11639" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82.proj%E2%82%81" class="Function">proj₁</a><a id="11644" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="11646" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82.proj%E2%82%82" class="Function">proj₂</a><a id="11651" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="11653" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">_,_</a><a id="11656" class="Symbol">)</a>

  <a id="11714" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Fun.rec%E2%82%82" class="Function">rec₂</a> <a id="11719" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11719" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="11721" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11721" class="Bound">c₀</a> <a id="11724" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11724" class="Bound">cₛ</a> <a id="11727" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11727" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="11729" class="Symbol">=</a>
      <a id="11737" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11738" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Fun.ite" class="Function">ite</a> <a id="11742" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11743" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a> <a id="11745" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_" class="Datatype Operator">×</a> <a id="11747" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11719" class="Bound">C</a><a id="11748" class="Symbol">)</a>
           <a id="11761" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11762" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95.zero" class="InductiveConstructor">zero</a> <a id="11767" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="11769" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11721" class="Bound">c₀</a><a id="11771" class="Symbol">)</a>
           <a id="11784" class="Symbol">(λ</a> <a id="11787" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11788" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11788" class="Bound">p</a> <a            <a id="11854" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11727" class="Bound">n</a><a id="11855" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Now, we need to establish the propositional equality between these two
definitions of recursor, i.e, between `rec` and `rec₂`. Let's use
induction to prove that.

      <a id="12745" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12681" class="Function">u</a> <a id="12747" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12749" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Fun%E2%82%82.ap-proj%E2%82%82" class="Function">ap-proj₂</a>  <a id="12759" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="12760" class="Argument">A</a> <a id="12762" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12764" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a><a id="12765" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="12767" class="Argument">B</a> <a id="12769" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12771" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12384" class="Bound">C</a><a id="12772" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="12774" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="12775" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#ex1-4.proof" class="Function">proof</a> <a id="12781" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12384" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="12783" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12386" class="Bound">c₀</a> <a id="12786" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12389" class="Bound">cₛ</a> <a id="12789" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12397" class="Bound">n</a><a id="12790" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>


### Exercise 1.5

<div class="exercise">

Show that if we define

  $$A+B :\equiv \sum\limits_{(x : \mathbbbold{2})} \mathsf{rec}_{\mathbbbold{2}} (\mathcal{U}, A , B, x),$$

then we can give a definition of $$\ind\limits_{A + B}$$ for which the
definitional equalities holds.

</div>

To solve this problem, let us introduce the $$\mathcal{2}$$ type, that is, the
type with two constructors also called **Bool**. The constructors are also called
false and true respectively.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="13295" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="𝟚-Def₁" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81" class="Module">𝟚-Def₁</a> <a id="13309" class="Keyword">where</a>

  <a id="13318" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="𝟚-Def₁.𝟚" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a> <a id="13325" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="13327" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="13331" class="Keyword">where</a>
    <a id="𝟚-Def₁.𝟚.𝟘" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%98" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟘</a> <a id="13343" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="13345" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a>
    <a id="𝟚-Def₁.𝟚.𝟙" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%99" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟙</a> <a id="13353" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="13355" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Now, let's try to define the recursor for this coproduct, and later,
we'll try the dependent version of it to complete the exercise.

Notice how the recursor of the coproduct matches with the elimination
rule of the disjunction conective also called *case analysis*. That's follows from the
[**propositions-as-types**](https://ncatlab.org/nlab/show/propositions+as+types).

![path](/assets/latexit-images/disj-elimination.png)

Finally, the induction principle for the coproduct:

### Exercise 1.6

<div class="exercise" id="ex-1.6">
Show that if we define $$A \times B :≡ \prod_{x:\mathbf{2}}\mathsf{rec}_{\mathbf{2}}\ (\mathcal{U}\, A\, B\, x)$$,
then we can give a definition of $$\mathsf{ind}_{A\times B}$$ for which the definitional
equalities propositionally (i.e. using equality types).
</div>

### Exercise 1.8

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.8">

Define multiplication and exponentiation using $$\mathsf{rec}{\mathbb{N}}$$.
Verify that $$(\mathbb{N},+,0,\times,1)$$ is a semiring using only
$$\ind{\mathbb{N}}$$.

</div>

### Exercise 1.9

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.9">

Define the type family $$\mathsf{Fin} : \mathbb{N} \to \mathcal{U}$$ mentioned
at the end of Section 1.3, and the dependent function $$\mathsf{fmax} :
\prod_{n:\mathbb{N}} \mathsf{Fin}(n+1)$$ mentioned in Section 1.4.
</div>

### Exercise 1.11

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.11">
Show that for any type $$A$$, we have $$\neg\neg\neg A \to \neg A$$.
</div>

### Exercise 1.16

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.16">
Show that addition of natural numbers is commutative:
<p class="equation">
$$
\prod\limits_{i,j : \mathbb{N}}\ (i + j = j + i).
$$
</p>
</div>

## Chapter 2

### Exercise 2.6

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-2.6">
Prove that if $$p : x \equiv y$$, then the function
$$(p \cdot -) : (y \equiv z) \to (x \equiv z)$$ is an equivalence.
</div>

### Exercise 2.10

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-2.10">
Prove that ∑-types are associative, in that for any $$A : \mathcal{U}$$
and families $$B : A  \to U$$ and $$C : \sum_{(x : A)} B(x) \to \mathcal{U}$$,
we have
<p class="equation">
$$\sum\limits_{(x : A)} \sum\limits_{(y : B(x))} C((x,y)) \simeq \sum\limits_{p : \sum_{x:A} B(x)} C(p)$$.
</p>
</div>

<div class="proof" id="proof-2.10">
Solution.<br/>
We can prove that the following functions $$f$$ and $$g$$ are inverses.

<p class="equation">
$$\sum\limits_{(x : A)} \sum\limits_{(y : B(x))} C((x,y)) \overset{f}{\underset{g}{\rightleftarrows}} \sum\limits_{p : \sum_{x:A} B(x)} C(p)$$.
</p>
defined by $$f(a,b,c) :\equiv ((a,b),c)$$, $$g(z,c) :\equiv (\mathsf{proj}_1 z,\mathsf{proj}_{2} z, c)$$.<br/>
Indeed,
<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
(f \circ g) (z, c) &:\equiv f (g (z,c))\\
&:\equiv f\,(\mathsf{proj}_1 z,\mathsf{proj}_{2} z, c)\\
&:\equiv ((\mathsf{proj}_1 z,\mathsf{proj}_{2} z), c)
\end{align*}
$$
</p>
</div>

        <a id="20206" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="20208" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20209" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20209" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="20211" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="20213" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3" class="Record">Σ</a> <a id="20215" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20157" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="20217" class="Symbol">(λ</a> <a id="20220" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20220" class="Bound">a</a> <a id="20222" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="20224" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3" class="Record">Σ</a> <a id="20226" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20227" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20167" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="20229" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20220" class="Bound">a</a><a id="20230" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="20232" class="Symbol">(λ</a> <a id="20235" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20235" class="Bound">b</a> <a id="20237" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="20239" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20181" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="20241" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20242" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20220" class="Bound">a</a> <a id="20244" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="20246" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20235" class="Bound">b</a><a id="20247" class="Symbol">))))</a>

### Exercise 2.13

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-2.13">
Show that $$(2 \simeq 2) \simeq 2$$.
</div>


### Exercise 2.14

{: .exercise}

  Suppose we add to type theory [the equality reflection
  rule](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IlfQjWqrK6I) which says that if there is
  an element $$p : \mathsf{Id}(x,y) $$, then in fact $$ x :\equiv y$$. Prove
  that for any $$p : \mathsf{Id}(x,x)$$ we have $$p :\equiv \mathsf{refl}_x$$.

{: .proof}
  Proof.<br/>
  By means of base path induction, we show that
  $$\mathsf{Id}(p,\mathsf{refl_{x}})$$. Let be $$a : A$$ and $$C :\equiv
  \prod_{x : A} \prod_{p : a \equiv x }\ p \equiv \mathsf{refl}_{x}$$. It
  sufficies to show and inhabitant of $$C(x, \mathsf{refl}_{x})$$, and it is,
  $$\mathsf{refl}_{\mathsf{refl}_x} : \mathsf{refl}_x \equiv \mathsf{refl}_x$$.
  By equation reflection rule, since que got an inhabitant of $$p \equiv
  \mathsf{refl}_x$$, these are judgemental equal, $$p :\equiv \mathsf{refl}_x$$.
  

### Exercise 2.17

<div class="exercise">
<ul>
  <li> Show that if $$A \simeq A$$  and $$B \simeq B'$$, then $$(A\times B) \simeq (A'\times B')$$. </li>
  <li> Give two proofs of this fact, one using univalence and one not using it, and show that the two proofs are equal.</li>
  <li> Formulate and prove analogous results for the other type formers: $$\Sigma$$, $$\to$$, $$\Pi$$, and $$+$$. </li>
</ul>
</div>



## Chapter 3

To solve the following exercises, let us recall a few things:

- The *set* definition in HoTT:

A type $$A$$ is a **set** if for all $$x, y : A$$ and
all $$p, q : x \equiv y$$, we have $$ p \equiv q$$. In a proposition
we have

$$
\mathsf{isSet}(A) :\equiv \prod\limits_{(x,y : A)}\prod\limits_{(p,q : x \equiv y)} (p \equiv q).
$$

- The type for equivalence from $$A$$ to $$B$$

$$
  (A \simeq B) :\equiv \sum\limits_{f : A \to B} \mathsf{isequiv}(f),
$$

where

$$
\mathsf{isequiv(f)} :\equiv
  \left (\sum\limits_{g : B \to A} (f \circ g \sim \mathsf{id}_{B})\right) \times
  \left (\sum\limits_{h : B \to A} (h \circ f \sim \mathsf{id}_{A})\right)
$$

- The homotopy concept:

Let $$f , g : \prod\limits_{(x:A)} P(x)$$ be two sections of a
type family $$P : A \to \mathcal{U}$$. A **homotopy** from $$f$$ to $$g$$
is a dependent function of type

$$
(f \sim g) :\equiv \prod\limits_{x : A} (f(x) \equiv g(x)).
$$

### Exercise 3.1

<div class="exercise">
Prove that if $$A\simeq B$$ and $$A$$ is a set, then so is $$B$$.
</div>


<div class="proof" id="proof-3.1">
Proof 1.<br/>
Let be $$x,y : B$$ and $$p : x \equiv_{B} y$$ and $$q : x \equiv_{B} y$$.
We need to prove $$ p \equiv q$$.<br/>
Since $$A\simeq B$$ then there is a function $$f : A \to B$$ and some
$$g : B \to A$$ such that $$f \circ g \sim id_{B}$$.
Using this function $$g$$ over the path $$p$$ we get
$$\mathsf{ap}_{g} p : g x \equiv_{A} g y$$.
We do the same but this time over the path $$q$$, that is,
$$\mathsf{ap}_{g} q : g x \equiv_{A} g y$$.
Because of $$A$$ is a set, we have a new path called
$$m :\mathsf{ap}_{g} p \equiv_{gx \equiv_{A} gy} \mathsf{ap}_{g} q$$. <br/>

Now, an action over this path $$m$$
using the function $$\mathsf{ap}_{f} : x \equiv_{A} y \to f x \equiv_{B} f y$$
will give us


$$
\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{ap}_{f}} m :
(\mathsf{ap}_{f}) (\mathsf{ap}_{g} p) \equiv (\mathsf{ap}_{f})  (\mathsf{ap}_{g} q).
$$


By the lemmas in Chapter 2, we do the following reasoning:

$$
\begin{align*}
(\mathsf{ap}_{f}) (\mathsf{ap}_{g} p) \equiv (\mathsf{ap}_{f})  (\mathsf{ap}_{g} q) &=
  \mathsf{ap}_{f \circ g} p \equiv \mathsf{ap}_{f \circ g} q\\
  &=(\text{transporting by using} f \sim g)\\
  &=\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{id}_{B}} p \equiv \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{id}_{B}} q\\
  &=p \equiv q.
\end{align*}
$$

Then, we have the inhabitant, $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{ap}_{f}} m : p \equiv q$$.
</div>

### Exercise 3.2

<div class="exercise">
Prove that if $$A$$ and $$B$$ are sets, then so is $$A+B$$.
</div>

To solve this exercise, we should take a look of some results from Chapter 2,
Section 2.12.

<div class="proof" id="proof-3.2">
Proof.<br/>

Let be $$x, y : A + B$$, and paths $$p : x \equiv y$$, $$q : x \equiv
y$$. Let's get a path $$p \equiv q$$.  We proceed by case analysis. If
$$x :\equiv \mathsf{inl} a$$ and $$y :\equiv \mathsf{inl} b$$, for
some $$a, b : A$$ then $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p : a
\equiv_{A} b$$ and $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} q : a \equiv_{A}
b$$.

Since $$A$$ is a set, there is a path between these last two terms,
this is, $$m : \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p \equiv
\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} q$$.  Now, an action over this path
$$m$$ using the $$\mathsf{inl}$$ function give us:
$$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}} m : \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
(\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p) \equiv \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
(\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} q)$$.<br/>

By path algebra we get $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
m : p \equiv q$$ since $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
(\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p) \equiv p$$.<br/> Following the
same reasoning, we prove the case $$x :\equiv \mathsf{inr} a$$ and $$y
:\equiv \mathsf{inr} b$$.  For the latest cases, $$x :\equiv
\mathsf{inl} a$$ and $$y :\equiv \mathsf{inr} b$$ and $$x :\equiv
\mathsf{inr} a$$ and $$y :\equiv \mathsf{inl} b$$, we use the
encode-decode method to derive a proof term for 𝟘 from
$$p$$ and $$q$$. Then, we may conclude anything we wish, that is, $$p
\equiv q$$.
</div>

In Agda.

  <a id="26715" class="Comment">-- ind : {A B : Set}</a>
  <a id="26738" class="Comment">--     → (C : A + B → Set)</a>
  <a id="26767" class="Comment">--     → ((x : A) → C (inl x))</a>
  <a id="26800" class="Comment">--     → ((x : B) → C (inr x))</a>
  <a id="26833" class="Comment">--     → (x : A + B) → C x</a>
  <a id="26862" class="Comment">-- ind C f g c x = {!   !}</a>

### Exercise 3.3

<div class="exercise">
Prove that if $$ A $$ is a set and $$B : A \to \mathcal{U}$$
is a type family such that $$B(x)$$ is a set for all
$$x : A$$, then $$\Sigma\limits_{(x:A)}\ B(x)$$ is a set.
</div>

### Exercise 3.4

<div class="exercise">
Show that $$A$$ is a mere proposition if and only
if $$A\to A$$ is contractible.
</div>
